   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Voiceless dental and alveolar stops
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">

        </th>
       </tr>

          </span>

          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        voiceless alveolar stop
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound used in many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speech_communication" title="Speech communication">
        spoken
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       . The symbol in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       that represents voiceless
       <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
        dental
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
        alveolar
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_consonant" title="Postalveolar consonant">
        postalveolar
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Stop_consonant" title="Stop consonant">
        stops
       </a>
       is ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        t
       </span>
       ⟩, and the equivalent
       <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
        X-SAMPA
       </a>
       symbol is
       <code>
        t
       </code>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_stop" title="Voiceless dental stop">
        dental stop
       </a>
       can be distinguished with the underbridge diacritic, ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        t̪
       </span>
       ⟩, the postalveolar with a retraction line, ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        t̠
       </span>
       ⟩, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extensions_to_the_IPA" title="Extensions to the IPA">
        Extensions to the IPA
       </a>
       have a double underline diacritic which can be used to explicitly specify an alveolar pronunciation, ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        t͇
       </span>
       ⟩.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [t]
       </span>
       sound is a very common sound cross-linguistically;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibermanCooperShankweilerStuddert-Kennedy1967?_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibermanCooperShankweilerStuddert-Kennedy1967?-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the most common consonant phonemes of the world's languages are
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [t]
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [k]
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [p]
       </span>
       . Most languages have at least a plain
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [t]
       </span>
       , and some distinguish more than one variety. Some languages without a
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [t]
       </span>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_language" title="Hawaiian language">
        Hawaiian
       </a>
       (except for
       <a href="/wiki/Niihau" title="Niihau">
        Niʻihau
       </a>
       ; Hawaiian uses a
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_stop" title="Voiceless velar stop">
        voiceless velar stop
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [k]
       </span>
       for loanwords with
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [t]
       </span>
       ), colloquial
       <a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">
        Samoan
       </a>
       (which also lacks an
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [n]
       </span>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abau" title="Abau">
        Abau
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/N%C7%81ng_language" title="Nǁng language">
        Nǁng
       </a>
       of South Africa.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2007)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_dental_and_alveolar_stops&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Here are features of the voiceless alveolar stop:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Occlusive" title="Occlusive">
         occlusive
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by obstructing airflow in the vocal tract. Since the consonant is also oral, with no
        <a href="/wiki/Nasal_consonant" title="Nasal consonant">
         nasal outlet
        </a>
        , the airflow is blocked entirely, and the consonant is a
        <a href="/wiki/Stop_consonant" title="Stop consonant">
         stop
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        There are three specific variants of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [t]
        </span>
        :
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
           Dental
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue at the upper
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teeth" title="Teeth">
           teeth
          </a>
          , termed respectively
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">
            apical
           </a>
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Laminal_consonant" title="Laminal consonant">
            laminal
           </a>
          </i>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Denti-alveolar_consonant" title="Denti-alveolar consonant">
           Denti-alveolar
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with the blade of the tongue at the
          <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" title="Alveolar ridge">
           alveolar ridge
          </a>
          , and the tip of the tongue behind upper teeth.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
           Alveolar
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue at the alveolar ridge, termed respectively
          <i>
           apical
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           laminal
          </i>
          .
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiceless, which means it is produced without vibrations of the vocal cords. In some languages the vocal cords are actively separated, so it is always voiceless; in others the cords are lax, so that it may take on the voicing of adjacent sounds.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>

          [t̪ant̪]

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Variable">
        Variable
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_dental_and_alveolar_stops&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Variable">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2">
         Language
        </th>
        <th>
         Word
        </th>

       <tr>
        <td rowspan="3">
         <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
          English
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         Broad
         <a href="/wiki/South_African_English" title="South African English">
          South African
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELass2002120_42-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELass2002120-42">
           [42]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td rowspan="3">
         <span lang="en">
          <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">
           <i>
            <b>
             t
            </b>
            alk
           </i>
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [toːk]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td rowspan="3">
         'talk'
        </td>
        <td rowspan="3">
         Laminal denti-alveolar for some speakers, alveolar for other speakers.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELass2002120_42-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELass2002120-42">
           [42]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEScobbieGordeevaMatthews20064_43-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEScobbieGordeevaMatthews20064-43">
           [43]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWells1982388_44-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWells1982388-44">
           [44]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Scottish_English" title="Scottish English">
          Scottish
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEScobbieGordeevaMatthews20064_43-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEScobbieGordeevaMatthews20064-43">
           [43]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [tʰɔk]
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Welsh_English" title="Welsh English">
          Welsh
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWells1982388_44-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWells1982388-44">
           [44]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [tʰɒːk]
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
          German
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         Standard
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMangold200547_45-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMangold200547-45">
           [45]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="de">
           <a href="/wiki/German_orthography" title="German orthography">
            <i>
             <b>
              T
             </b>
             ochter
            </i>
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ˈtɔxtɐ]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'daughter'
        </td>
        <td>
         Varies between laminal denti-alveolar, laminal alveolar and apical alveolar.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMangold200547_45-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMangold200547-45">
           [45]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Standard_German_phonology" title="Standard German phonology">
          Standard German phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">
          Greek
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArvaniti200710_46-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArvaniti200710-46">
           [46]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span lang="el">
          <a href="/wiki/Greek_alphabet" title="Greek alphabet">
           <b>
            τ
           </b>
           ρία
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Greek" title="Romanization of Greek">
           <i>
            <b>
             t
            </b>
            ria
           </i>
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ˈtria]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'three'
        </td>
        <td>
         Varies between dental, laminal denti-alveolar and alveolar, depending on the environment.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArvaniti200710_46-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArvaniti200710-46">
           [46]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Modern_Greek_phonology" title="Modern Greek phonology">
          Modern Greek phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">
          Norwegian
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Urban_East_Norwegian" title="Urban East Norwegian">
          Urban East
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKristoffersen200022_47-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKristoffersen200022-47">
           [47]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="no">
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_alphabet" title="Norwegian alphabet">
            <i>
             <b>
              d
             </b>
             ans
            </i>
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [t̻ɑns]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'dance'
        </td>
        <td>
         Varies between laminal denti-alveolar and laminal alveolar. It is usually transcribed
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /d/
         </span>
         . It may be partially voiced
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [
          <a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_and_alveolar_stops#Alveolar" title="Voiced dental and alveolar stops">
           d̥
          </a>
          ]
         </span>
         , and it contrasts with voiceless aspirated form, which is usually transcribed
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /t/
         </span>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKristoffersen200022_47-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKristoffersen200022-47">
           [47]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_phonology" title="Norwegian phonology">
          Norwegian phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">
          Persian
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mah_48-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-mah-48">
           [48]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span lang="fa">
          <a href="/wiki/Persian_alphabet" title="Persian alphabet">
           توت
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [tut]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'berry'
        </td>
        <td>
         Varies between laminal denti-alveolar and apical alveolar.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mah_48-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-mah-48">
           [48]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Persian_phonology" title="Persian phonology">
          Persian phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">

          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="sk">
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovak_alphabet" title="Slovak alphabet">
            <i>
             <b>
              t
             </b>
             o
            </i>
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [t̻o̞]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'that'
        </td>
        <td>
         Varies between laminal denti-alveolar and laminal alveolar.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKráľ198872_49-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKráľ198872-49">
           [49]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPavlík200498–99_50-1">
